Bug Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n- `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java` — examined for entry point and buffer deallocation flow\n- `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java` — examined for batch draining and deallocate method\n- `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/ProducerBatch.java` — examined for batch structure\n- `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/record/MemoryRecordsBuilder.java` — examined for buffer lifecycle\n- `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/utils/ByteBufferOutputStream.java` — examined for underlying buffer management\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` at lines 357-444\n   - Messages appear on wrong topic when batches expire during network transmission\n\n2. **Called from**: User calls `producer.send(record)` → RecordAccumulator.append() → Accumulator drains batches → Sender sends requests\n\n3. **Bug triggered by**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` at lines 395-442\n   - The critical sequence that exposes the race condition\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n\n**Function**: `sendProducerData(long now)`\n\n**Lines**: 395-442 (execution sequence)\n\n**Critical Lines in Race Condition**:\n- Line 395: Batches drained from accumulator\n- Line 396: Batches added to inflight tracking\n- Line 406-408: Expired batches identified (including inflight batches)\n- Line 418: `failBatch()` called on expired batches → buffer deallocated\n- Line 442: `sendProduceRequests()` still sends ALL drained batches (including expired ones)\n\n### Explanation\n\nThe bug is a classic **Time-of-Check-Time-of-Use (TOCTOU) race condition**:\n\n1. **Line 395**: `accumulator.drain()` returns a map of batches ready to send\n   ```java\n   Map<Integer, List<ProducerBatch>> batches = this.accumulator.drain(metadataSnapshot, result.readyNodes, this.maxRequestSize, now);\n   ```\n\n2. **Line 396**: These batches are added to `inFlightBatches` to track them:\n   ```java\n   addToInflightBatches(batches);\n   ```\n\n3. **Lines 406-408**: The code checks for expired batches, including those just added to inflight:\n   ```java\n   List<ProducerBatch> expiredInflightBatches = getExpiredInflightBatches(now);\n   List<ProducerBatch> expiredBatches = this.accumulator.expiredBatches(now);\n   expiredBatches.addAll(expiredInflightBatches);\n   ```\n\n4. **Lines 415-423**: For each expired batch, `failBatch()` is called:\n   ```java\n   for (ProducerBatch expiredBatch : expiredBatches) {\n       String errorMessage = \"Expiring \" + expiredBatch.recordCount + \" record(s) for \" + expiredBatch.topicPartition\n           + \":\" + (now - expiredBatch.createdMs) + \" ms has passed since batch creation\";\n       failBatch(expiredBatch, new TimeoutException(errorMessage), false);\n       // ...\n   }\n   ```\n\n5. **Lines 835** (in `failBatch()` overload): The batch's buffer is deallocated:\n   ```java\n   maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n   // Which calls:\n   this.accumulator.deallocate(batch);\n   // Which returns the buffer to the pool:\n   free.deallocate(batch.buffer(), batch.initialCapacity());\n   ```\n\n6. **Line 442**: `sendProduceRequests()` is called with the ORIGINAL `batches` map, which still contains the expired batches:\n   ```java\n   sendProduceRequests(batches, now);\n   ```\n\n### The Race Condition\n\nThe `batches` map at line 442 contains **the same batch objects** that were expired and deallocated at line 423. The code does NOT remove the expired batches from the `batches` map before calling `sendProduceRequests()`.\n\nIn `sendProduceRequest()` (lines 864-916), when the expired batch's data is accessed:\n- Line 874: `MemoryRecords records = batch.records()`\n- Line 886: The records are added to the request\n\nAt this point, the underlying `ByteBuffer` of the batch has been returned to the `BufferPool` (line 1032 in RecordAccumulator.deallocate()). This buffer can now be:\n1. **Immediately reused** by another ProducerBatch being created on a different partition/topic\n2. **Modified** as the new batch writes records to it\n3. **Serialized to the network** as part of the new batch's request\n\nMeanwhile, the expired batch's buffer reference still points to this same underlying buffer. When the network layer serializes the original expired batch's request, it reads from a buffer that now contains data from the new batch, causing the **topic/partition fields in the produce request header to be corrupted**.\n\n### Why This Causes Wrong Topic Corruption\n\nThe produce request is structured as:\n1. **Request Header** (topic, partition) - serialized from the batch metadata\n2. **Message Payload** (key, value, headers) - stored in the batch's buffer\n\nThe CRC checksum covers only the message payload, not the request header. So:\n- The message CRC passes validation (it's from the correct source)\n- But the topic/partition in the request header has been corrupted by buffer reuse\n- Result: Message appears on the wrong topic\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe fix is to **remove expired batches from the `batches` map before calling `sendProduceRequests()`**, ensuring that deallocated buffers are never accessed.\n\n### Required Imports\nAdd to existing imports at top of Sender.java:\n```java\nimport java.util.HashSet;\nimport java.util.Set;\n```\n\n### Code Change\n\nLocation: `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n\n**Insert after line 408** (after `expiredBatches.addAll(expiredInflightBatches);`)\n\n```diff\n--- a/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n+++ b/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n@@ -406,6 +406,20 @@ private long sendProduceData(long now) {\n         List<ProducerBatch> expiredInflightBatches = getExpiredInflightBatches(now);\n         List<ProducerBatch> expiredBatches = this.accumulator.expiredBatches(now);\n         expiredBatches.addAll(expiredInflightBatches);\n+\n+        // Remove expired batches from the batches map to prevent race condition.\n+        // Expired batches have their buffers deallocated and returned to the pool.\n+        // We must ensure that sendProduceRequests() does not try to serialize\n+        // deallocated buffers, as they may be reused by new batches on different topics,\n+        // causing messages to appear on wrong topics.\n+        if (!expiredBatches.isEmpty()) {\n+            Set<ProducerBatch> expiredBatchSet = new HashSet<>(expiredBatches);\n+            for (List<ProducerBatch> batchList : batches.values()) {\n+                batchList.removeAll(expiredBatchSet);\n+            }\n+            batches.entrySet().removeIf(entry -> entry.getValue().isEmpty());\n+        }\n\n         // Reset the producer id if an expired batch has previously been sent to the broker. Also update the metrics\n         // for expired batches. see the documentation of @TransactionState.resetIdempotentProducerId to understand why\n```\n\n### Fix Explanation\n\nThe fix works by:\n1. Creating a `Set` of expired batch objects\n2. Iterating through all node-level batch lists in the `batches` map\n3. Removing any expired batches from these lists\n4. Cleaning up any empty node entries\n\nThis ensures that when `sendProduceRequests()` is called at line 442, it only processes batches that:\n- Have valid, non-deallocated buffers\n- Have not reached delivery timeout\n- Are safe to serialize and send to the network\n\n### Why This Fix Is Correct\n\n1. **Preserves error handling**: Expired batches are still failed via `failBatch()`, so users still get proper timeout exceptions\n2. **Prevents corruption**: No deallocated buffers are accessed by `sendProduceRequests()`\n3. **Thread-safe**: The expiration check and removal happen in the Sender thread before any network operations\n4. **Minimal overhead**: Set lookup is O(1), and expired batches are typically rare during normal operation\n5. **Idempotent**: Can safely be called even if there are no expired batches\n\n### Alternative Fix (Not Recommended)\n\nAn alternative would be to add an `isDone()` check in `sendProduceRequest()` before accessing the batch:\n\n```java\nfor (ProducerBatch batch : batches) {\n    if (batch.isDone()) {\n        continue;  // Skip already completed batches\n    }\n    // ... rest of the code\n}\n```\n\nHowever, this is **not recommended** because:\n- It's a band-aid that masks the root cause (expired batches being included in the send list)\n- It's less clear that expired batches should never be sent\n- It could hide other bugs where `isDone()` is true but the batch is still sent inappropriately\n- The proposed fix is more explicit and clearer about intent\n\n### Additional Note\n\nThe comment at line 192 in `Sender.java` is relevant:\n```java\n// expireBatches is called in Sender.sendProducerData, before client.poll.\n// The !batch.isDone() invariant should always hold.\n```\n\nThis comment suggests the original intent was that expired batches would NOT be in the send list. The proposed fix restores this invariant, which is the correct approach.\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\n### The Bug in One Sentence\nA race condition in `Sender.sendProducerData()` allows deallocated buffer pools to be reused while still being referenced by batches that are sent to the network, causing message data to be corrupted with metadata from subsequent batches on different topics.\n\n### The Fix in One Sentence\nRemove expired batches from the `batches` map after deallocating their buffers, but before calling `sendProduceRequests()`, ensuring no deallocated buffers are accessed by the network layer.\n\n### Verification Steps\nTo verify this fix resolves the issue:\n\n1. Create a test that:\n   - Creates a batch for topic A with long linger.ms\n   - Creates another batch for topic B immediately after\n   - Forces batch A to expire by advancing the clock\n   - Verifies that batch A is NOT sent to the network\n   - Verifies that the buffer reused by batch B doesn't contain corrupted topic information\n\n2. Run existing test suite to ensure no regressions:\n   ```bash\n   ./gradlew clients:test --tests SenderTest\n   ./gradlew clients:test --tests RecordAccumulatorTest\n   ```\n\n3. Integration test with realistic scenario:\n   - Use a real Kafka cluster\n   - Set `linger.ms=1000` and `delivery.timeout.ms=2000`\n   - Simulate network latency/broker restart to trigger batch expiry\n   - Verify messages don't appear on unintended topics\n\n## Detailed Call Stack\n\n### Key Method Call Path for the Bug\n\n```\nSender.run() (main thread)\n  ↓\nSender.runOnce() (line ~337)\n  ↓\nSender.sendProducerData(now) (line 357-444) ← CRITICAL METHOD\n  ├─ accumulator.drain() (line 395) ← Gets batches to send\n  ├─ addToInflightBatches() (line 396) ← Adds to tracking\n  ├─ getExpiredInflightBatches() (line 406) ← Checks expiry\n  ├─ accumulator.expiredBatches() (line 407) ← Gets expired\n  │\n  ├─ for expiredBatch in expiredBatches (lines 415-423)\n  │   └─ failBatch(expiredBatch, ...) (line 418)\n  │       └─ maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch() (line 835)\n  │           └─ accumulator.deallocate(batch) (line 174)\n  │               └─ free.deallocate(buffer, capacity) (line 1032)\n  │                   ← BUFFER RETURNED TO POOL ← CRITICAL\n  │\n  └─ sendProduceRequests(batches, now) (line 442) ← BUG: Still sends expired batches\n      └─ sendProduceRequest(..., entry.getValue()) (line 858)\n          └─ for batch in batches (line 872)\n              ├─ batch.records() (line 874) ← Accesses deallocated buffer\n              └─ client.send(request) (line 914) ← Sends corrupted request\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Timeline (Normal Case - No Race Condition)\n1. User calls `producer.send(topicA, record1)`\n2. Record accumulates in RecordAccumulator\n3. `sendProducerData()` drains batches for topicA\n4. Batch is sent to network correctly\n\n### Execution Timeline (Race Condition Case)\n1. User calls `producer.send(topicA, record1)` and `producer.send(topicB, record2)`\n2. Both records accumulate\n3. `sendProducerData()` is called at `now = T0`\n4. **T0 + Δ1**: Batch for topicA is drained and added to inflight\n5. **T0 + Δ2**: Batch for topicB is drained and added to inflight\n6. **T0 + Δ3**: System clock advances (simulate delay/network lag)\n7. **T0 + Δ4**: Check for expired batches\n   - Batch for topicA has **createdMs = T0 - (linger.ms + 100ms)** (was lingering)\n   - Now **now = T0 + 500ms**, so it exceeds delivery timeout\n   - `getExpiredInflightBatches()` finds topicA batch as expired\n8. **T0 + Δ5**: `failBatch(topicA_batch)` is called\n   - `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` deallocates topicA_batch's buffer\n   - Buffer returned to pool, marked as available\n9. **T0 + Δ6**: New user call: `producer.send(topicC, record3)`\n   - RecordAccumulator allocates a new batch from the pool\n   - **Gets the same ByteBuffer** that was just deallocated from topicA_batch\n   - Writes topicC records to this buffer\n10. **T0 + Δ7**: `sendProduceRequests()` is called\n    - Includes the topicA_batch in the list (it wasn't removed from `batches` map)\n    - Tries to send topicA_batch.records()\n    - The buffer now contains topicC data and metadata\n    - **Request is serialized with topicA batch object metadata but topicC buffer content**\n    - Message intended for topicA appears on topicC\n\n### Why This Happens In Bursts\n\nThe symptom notes state: \"messages published to topic A occasionally appear on topic B instead. The corruption is rare but occurs in bursts, typically during broker restarts or network disruptions.\"\n\nThis makes sense because:\n- **Bursts during broker restarts**: When a broker restarts, in-flight batches may experience timeout conditions more frequently\n- **Bursts during network disruptions**: Batches timeout while requests are in flight, but the network layer hasn't fully transmitted them yet\n- **Rare occurrences**: The race condition requires:\n  1. A batch to expire (reach delivery timeout)\n  2. While another batch is being created and allocated from the pool\n  3. Before the expired batch's request is fully serialized to the network\n  4. This is a tight timing window, hence \"occasional\"\n\n### Buffer Lifecycle Issue\n\nThe core issue is the **buffer lifecycle mismatch**:\n- **BufferPool assumption**: Once `deallocate()` is called, the buffer is no longer in use\n- **Sender assumption**: Batches in the `batches` map are still valid after expiration check\n- **Result**: The buffer can be reused while the Sender still references it\n\n### Why CRC Passes\n\nThe Kafka protocol structure has:\n- **Per-record CRC**: Covers key, value, headers, attributes, timestamp\n- **Does NOT cover**: Topic name, partition number (in request header)\n\nSo when a message is redirected to the wrong topic:\n1. The per-record CRC still validates (it covers the message content, which is correct)\n2. But the request header (topic/partition) has been corrupted\n3. The message successfully writes to the wrong topic\n4. This is why the corruption goes undetected at the record level\n\n## Prevention and Related Code\n\nThe fix could also be implemented by:\n1. **Removing batches from inflight when expired**: Have `getExpiredInflightBatches()` also remove from the original `batches` map\n2. **Deferring sendProduceRequests**: Only include non-expired batches when calling `sendProduceRequests()`\n3. **Marking batches**: Flag batches as \"deallocated\" and skip them in `sendProduceRequests()`\n\nThe cleanest approach is **Option 1** (proposed above): Remove expired batches from the `batches` map after deallocating them but before sending, ensuring the contract is clear and failures are fail-safe.\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":111,"oldLines":9,"newStart":111,"newLines":10,"lines":[" Add to existing imports at top of Sender.java:"," ```java"," import java.util.HashSet;","-import java.util.Set;"," ```"," ","+Note: `Set` is already imported in the file (line 43), and `List`, `Map`, `HashMap`, `ArrayList` are also already imported.","+"," ### Code Change"," "," Location: `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`"]}],"userModified":false,"replaceAll":false}}

batch's buffer is deallocated:\n    67→   ```java\n    68→   maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n    69→   // Which calls:\n    70→   this.accumulator.deallocate(batch);\n    71→   // Which returns the buffer to the pool:\n    72→   free.deallocate(batch.buffer(), batch.initialCapacity());\n    73→   ```\n    74→\n    75→6. **Line 442**: `sendProduceRequests()` is called with the ORIGINAL `batches` map, which still contains the expired batches:\n    76→   ```java\n    77→   sendProduceRequests(batches, now);\n    78→   ```\n    79→\n    80→### The Race Condition\n    81→\n    82→The `batches` map at line 442 contains **the same batch objects** that were expired and deallocated at line 423. The code does NOT remove the expired batches from the `batches` map before calling `sendProduceRequests()`.\n    83→\n    84→In `sendProduceRequest()` (lines 864-916), when the expired batch's data is accessed:\n    85→- Line 874: `MemoryRecords records = batch.records()`\n    86→- Line 886: The records are added to the request\n    87→\n    88→At this point, the underlying `ByteBuffer` of the batch has been returned to the `BufferPool` (line 1032 in RecordAccumulator.deallocate()). This buffer can now be:\n    89→1. **Immediately reused** by another ProducerBatch being created on a different partition/topic\n    90→2. **Modified** as the new batch writes records to it\n    91→3. **Serialized to the network** as part of the new batch's request\n    92→\n    93→Meanwhile, the expired batch's buffer reference still points to this same underlying buffer. When the network layer serializes the original expired batch's request, it reads from a buffer that now contains data from the new batch, causing the **topic/partition fields in the produce request header to be corrupted**.\n    94→\n    95→### Why This Causes Wrong Topic Corruption\n    96→\n    97→The produce request is structured as:\n    98→1. **Request Header** (topic, partition) - serialized from the batch metadata\n    99→2. **Message Payload** (key, value, headers) - stored in the batch's buffer\n   100→\n   101→The CRC checksum covers only the message payload, not the request header. So:\n   102→- The message CRC passes validation (it's from the correct source)\n   103→- But the topic/partition in the request header has been corrupted by buffer reuse\n   104→- Result: Message appears on the wrong topic\n   105→\n   106→## Proposed Fix\n   107→\n   108→The fix is to **remove expired batches from the `batches` map before calling `sendProduceRequests()`**, ensuring that deallocated buffers are never accessed.\n   109→\n   110→### Required Imports\n   111→Add to existing imports at top of Sender.java:\n   112→```java\n   113→import java.util.HashSet;\n   114→```\n   115→\n   116→Note: `Set` is already imported in the file (line 43), and `List`, `Map`, `HashMap`, `ArrayList` are also already imported.\n   117→\n   118→### Code Change\n   119→\n   120→Location: `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n   121→\n   122→**Insert after line 408** (after `expiredBatches.addAll(expiredInflightBatches);`)\n   123→\n   124→```diff\n   125→--- a/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n   126→+++ b/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n   127→@@ -406,6 +406,20 @@ private long sendProduceData(long now) {\n   128→         List<ProducerBatch> expiredBatches.addAll(expiredInflightBatches);\n   131→+\n   132→+        // Remove expired batches from the batches map to prevent race condition.\n   133→+        // Expired batches have their previously been sent to the broker. Also update the metrics\n   146→         // for expired batches. see the documentation of @TransactionState.resetIdempotentProducerId to understand why\n   147→```\n   148→\n   149→### Fix Explanation\n   150→\n   151→The fix works by:\n   152→1. Creating a `Set` of expired batch objects\n   153→2. Iterating through all node-level batch lists in the `batches` map\n   154→3. Removing any expired batches from these lists\n   155→4. Cleaning up any empty node entries\n   156→\n   157→This ensures that when `sendProduceRequests()` is called at line 442, it only processes batches that:\n   158→- Have valid, non-deallocated buffers\n   159→- Have not reached delivery timeout\n   160→- Are safe to serialize and send to the network\n   161→\n   162→### Why This Fix Is Correct\n   163→\n   164→1. **Preserves error handling**: Expired batches are still failed via `failBatch()`, so users still get proper timeout exceptions\n   165→2. **Prevents corruption**: No deallocated buffers are accessed by `sendProduceRequests()`\n   166→3. **Thread-safe**: The expiration check and removal happen in the Sender thread before any network operations\n   167→4. **Minimal overhead**: Set lookup is O(1), and expired batches are typically rare during normal operation\n   168→5. **Idempotent**: Can safely be called even if there are no expired batches\n   169→\n   170→### Alternative Fix (Not Recommended)\n   171→\n   172→An alternative would be to add an `isDone()` check in `sendProduceRequest()` before accessing the batch:\n   173→\n   174→```java\n   175→for (ProducerBatch batch : batches) {\n   176→    if (batch.isDone()) {\n   177→        continue; The proposed fix restores this invariant, which is the correct approach.\n   198→\n   199→---\n   200→\n   201→## Summary\n   202→\n   203→### The Bug in One Sentence\n   204→A race condition in `Sender.sendProducerData()` allows deallocated buffer pools to be reused while still being referenced by batches that are sent to the network, causing message data to be corrupted with metadata from subsequent batches on different topics.\n   205→\n   206→### The Fix in One Sentence\n   207→Remove expired batches from the `batches` map after deallocating their buffers, but before calling `sendProduceRequests()`, ensuring no deallocated buffers are accessed by the network layer.\n   208→\n   209→### Verification Steps\n   210→To verify this fix resolves the issue:\n   211→\n   212→1. (line 418)\n   248→  │       └─ maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch() (line 835)\n   249→  │           └─ accumulator.deallocate(batch) (line 174)\n   250→  │               └─ free.deallocate(buffer, capacity) (line 1032)\n   251→  │                   ← BUFFER RETURNED TO POOL ← CRITICAL\n   252→  │\n   253→  └─ sendProduceRequests(batches, now) (line 442) ← BUG: Still sends expired batches\n   254→      └─ sendProduceRequest(..., entry.getValue()) (line 858)\n   255→          └─ for batch in batches (line 872)\n   256→              ├─ batch.records() (line 874) ← Accesses deallocated buffer\n   257→              └─ client.send(request) (line 914) ← Sends corrupted request\n   258→```\n   259→\n   260→## Analysis\n   261→\n   262→### Execution Timeline (Normal Case - No Race Condition)\n   263→1. User calls `producer.send(topicA, record1)`\n   264→2. Record accumulates in RecordAccumulator\n   265→3. `sendProducerData()` drains batches for topicA\n   266→4. Batch is sent to network correctly\n   267→\n   268→### Execution Timeline (Race Condition Case)\n   269→1. User calls `producer.send(topicA, record1)` and `producer.send(topicB, record2)`\n   270→2. Both records accumulate\n   271→3. `sendProducerData()` is called at `now = T0`\n   272→4. **T0 + Δ1**: Batch for topicA is drained and added to inflight\n   273→5. **T0 + Δ2**: Batch for topicB is drained and added to inflight\n   274→6. **T0 + Δ3**: System clock advances (simulate delay/network lag)\n   275→7. **T0 + Δ4**: Check for expired batches\n   276→   - Batch for topicA has **createdMs = T0 - (linger.ms + 100ms)** (was lingering)\n   277→   - Now **now = T0 + 500ms**, so it exceeds delivery timeout\n   278→   - `getExpiredInflightBatches()` finds topicA batch as expired\n   279→8. **T0 + Δ5**: `failBatch(topicA_batch)` is called\n   280→   - `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` deallocates topicA_batch's buffer\n   281→   - Buffer returned to pool, marked as available\n   282→9. **T0 + Δ6**: New user call: `producer.send(topicC, record3)`\n   283→   - RecordAccumulator allocates a new batch from the pool\n   284→   - **Gets the same ByteBuffer** that was just deallocated from topicA_batch\n   285→   - Writes topicC records to this buffer\n   286→10. **T0 + Δ7**: `sendProduceRequests()` is called\n   287→    - Includes the topicA_batch in the list (it wasn't removed from `batches` map)\n   288→    - Tries to send topicA_batch.records()\n   289→    - The buffer now contains topicC data and metadata\n   290→    - **Request is serialized with topicA batch object metadata but topicC buffer content**\n   291→    - Message intended for topicA appears on topicC\n   292→\n   293→### Why This Happens In Bursts\n   294→\n   295→The symptom notes state: \"messages published to topic A occasionally appear on topic B instead. The corruption is rare but occurs in bursts, typically during broker restarts or network disruptions.\"\n   296→\n   297→This makes sense because:\n   298→- **Bursts during broker restarts**: When a broker restarts, in-flight batches may experience timeout conditions more frequently\n   299→- **Bursts during network disruptions**: Batches timeout while requests are in flight, but the network layer hasn't fully transmitted them yet\n   300→- **Rare occurrences**: The race condition requires:\n   301→  1. A batch to expire (reach delivery timeout)\n   302→  2. While another batch is being created and allocated from the pool\n   303→  3. Before the expired batch's request is fully serialized to the network\n   304→  4. This is a tight timing window, hence \"occasional\"\n   305→\n   306→### Buffer Lifecycle Issue\n   307→\n   308→The core issue is the **buffer lifecycle mismatch**:\n   309→- **BufferPool assumption**: Once `deallocate()` is called, the buffer is no longer in use\n   310→- **Sender assumption**: Batches in the `batches` map are still valid after expiration check\n   311→- **Result**: The buffer can be reused while the Sender still references it\n   312→\n   313→### Why CRC Passes\n   314→\n   315→The Kafka protocol structure has:\n   316→- **Per-record CRC**: Covers key, value, headers, attributes, timestamp\n   317→- **Does NOT cover**: Topic name, partition number (in request header)\n   318→\n   319→So when a message is redirected to the wrong topic:\n   320→1. The per-record CRC still validates (it covers the message content, which is correct)\n   321→2. But the request header (topic/partition) has been corrupted\n   322→3. The message successfully writes to the wrong topic\n   323→4. This is why the corruption goes undetected at the record level\n   324→\n   325→## Prevention and Related Code\n   326→\n   327→The fix could also be implemented by:\n   328→1. **Removing batches from inflight when expired**: Have `getExpiredInflightBatches()` also remove from the original `batches` map\n   329→2. **Deferring sendProduceRequests**: Only include non-expired batches when calling `sendProduceRequests()`\n   330→3. **Marking batches**: Flag batches as \"deallocated\" and skip them in `sendProduceRequests()`\n   331→\n   332→The cleanest approach is **Option 1** (proposed above): Remove expired batches from the `batches` map after deallocating them but before sending, ensuring the contract is clear and failures are fail-safe.\n   333→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Bug Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n- `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java` — examined for entry point and buffer deallocation flow\n- `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java` — examined for batch draining and deallocate method\n- `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/ProducerBatch.java` — examined for batch structure\n- `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/record/MemoryRecordsBuilder.java` — examined for buffer lifecycle\n- `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/utils/ByteBufferOutputStream.java` — examined for underlying buffer management\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` at lines 357-444\n   - Messages appear on wrong topic when batches expire during network transmission\n\n2. **Called from**: User calls `producer.send(record)` → RecordAccumulator.append() → Accumulator drains batches → Sender sends requests\n\n3. **Bug triggered by**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` at lines 395-442\n   - The critical sequence that exposes the race condition\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n\n**Function**: `sendProducerData(long now)`\n\n**Lines**: 395-442 (execution sequence)\n\n**Critical Lines in Race Condition**:\n- Line 395: Batches drained from accumulator\n- Line 396: Batches added to inflight tracking\n- Line 406-408: Expired batches identified (including inflight batches)\n- Line 418: `failBatch()` called on expired batches → buffer deallocated\n- Line 442: `sendProduceRequests()` still sends ALL drained batches (including expired ones)\n\n### Explanation\n\nThe bug is a classic **Time-of-Check-Time-of-Use (TOCTOU) race condition**:\n\n1. **Line 395**: `accumulator.drain()` returns a map of batches ready to send\n   ```java\n   Map<Integer, List<ProducerBatch>> batches = this.accumulator.drain(metadataSnapshot, result.readyNodes, this.maxRequestSize, now);\n   ```\n\n2. **Line 396**: These batches are added to `inFlightBatches` to track them:\n   ```java\n   addToInflightBatches(batches);\n   ```\n\n3. **Lines 406-408**: The code checks for expired batches, including those just added to inflight:\n   ```java\n   List<ProducerBatch> expiredInflightBatches = getExpiredInflightBatches(now);\n   List<ProducerBatch> expiredBatches = this.accumulator.expiredBatches(now);\n   expiredBatches.addAll(expiredInflightBatches);\n   ```\n\n4. **Lines 415-423**: For each expired batch, `failBatch()` is called:\n   ```java\n   for (ProducerBatch expiredBatch : expiredBatches) {\n       String errorMessage = \"Expiring \" + expiredBatch.recordCount + \" record(s) for \" + expiredBatch.topicPartition\n           + \":\" + (now - expiredBatch.createdMs) + \" ms has passed since batch creation\";\n       failBatch(expiredBatch, new TimeoutException(errorMessage), false);\n       // ...\n   }\n   ```\n\n5. **Lines 835** (in `failBatch()` overload): The batch's buffer is deallocated:\n   ```java\n   maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n   // Which calls:\n   this.accumulator.deallocate(batch);\n   // Which returns the buffer to the pool:\n   free.deallocate(batch.buffer(), batch.initialCapacity());\n   ```\n\n6. **Line 442**: `sendProduceRequests()` is called with the ORIGINAL `batches` map, which still contains the expired batches:\n   ```java\n   sendProduceRequests(batches, now);\n   ```\n\n### The Race Condition\n\nThe `batches` map at line 442 contains **the same batch objects** that were expired and deallocated at line 423. The code does NOT remove the expired batches from the `batches` map before calling `sendProduceRequests()`.\n\nIn `sendProduceRequest()` (lines 864-916), when the expired batch's data is accessed:\n- Line 874: `MemoryRecords records = batch.records()`\n- Line 886: The records are added to the request\n\nAt this point, the underlying `ByteBuffer` of the batch has been returned to the `BufferPool` (line 1032 in RecordAccumulator.deallocate()). This buffer can now be:\n1. **Immediately reused** by another ProducerBatch being created on a different partition/topic\n2. **Modified** as the new batch writes records to it\n3. **Serialized to the network** as part of the new batch's request\n\nMeanwhile, the expired batch's buffer reference still points to this same underlying buffer. When the network layer serializes the original expired batch's request, it reads from a buffer that now contains data from the new batch, causing the **topic/partition fields in the produce request header to be corrupted**.\n\n### Why This Causes Wrong Topic Corruption\n\nThe produce request is structured as:\n1. **Request Header** (topic, partition) - serialized from the batch metadata\n2. **Message Payload** (key, value, headers) - stored in the batch's buffer\n\nThe CRC checksum covers only the message payload, not the request header. So:\n- The message CRC passes validation (it's from the correct source)\n- But the topic/partition in the request header has been corrupted by buffer reuse\n- Result: Message appears on the wrong topic\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe fix is to **remove expired batches from the `batches` map before calling `sendProduceRequests()`**, ensuring that deallocated buffers are never accessed.\n\n### Required Imports\nAdd to existing imports at top of Sender.java:\n```java\nimport java.util.HashSet;\n```\n\nNote: `Set` is already imported in the file (line 43), and `List`, `Map`, `HashMap`, `ArrayList` are also already imported.\n\n### Code Change\n\nLocation: `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n\n**Insert after line 408** (after `expiredBatches.addAll(expiredInflightBatches);`)\n\n```diff\n--- a/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n+++ b/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n@@ -406,6 +406,20 @@ private long sendProduceData(long now) {\n         List<ProducerBatch> expiredInflightBatches = getExpiredInflightBatches(now);\n         List<ProducerBatch> expiredBatches = this.accumulator.expiredBatches(now);\n         expiredBatches.addAll(expiredInflightBatches);\n+\n+        // Remove expired batches from the batches map to prevent race condition.\n+        // Expired batches have their buffers deallocated and returned to the pool.\n+        // We must ensure that sendProduceRequests() does not try to serialize\n+        // deallocated buffers, as they may be reused by new batches on different topics,\n+        // causing messages to appear on wrong topics.\n+        if (!expiredBatches.isEmpty()) {\n+            Set<ProducerBatch> expiredBatchSet = new HashSet<>(expiredBatches);\n+            for (List<ProducerBatch> batchList : batches.values()) {\n+                batchList.removeAll(expiredBatchSet);\n+            }\n+            batches.entrySet().removeIf(entry -> entry.getValue().isEmpty());\n+        }\n\n         // Reset the producer id if an expired batch has previously been sent to the broker. Also update the metrics\n         // for expired batches. see the documentation of @TransactionState.resetIdempotentProducerId to understand why\n```\n\n### Fix Explanation\n\nThe fix works by:\n1. Creating a `Set` of expired batch objects\n2. Iterating through all node-level batch lists in the `batches` map\n3. Removing any expired batches from these lists\n4. Cleaning up any empty node entries\n\nThis ensures that when `sendProduceRequests()` is called at line 442, it only processes batches that:\n- Have valid, non-deallocated buffers\n- Have not reached delivery timeout\n- Are safe to serialize and send to the network\n\n### Why This Fix Is Correct\n\n1. **Preserves error handling**: Expired batches are still failed via `failBatch()`, so users still get proper timeout exceptions\n2. **Prevents corruption**: No deallocated buffers are accessed by `sendProduceRequests()`\n3. **Thread-safe**: The expiration check and removal happen in the Sender thread before any network operations\n4. **Minimal overhead**: Set lookup is O(1), and expired batches are typically rare during normal operation\n5. **Idempotent**: Can safely be called even if there are no expired batches\n\n### Alternative Fix (Not Recommended)\n\nAn alternative would be to add an `isDone()` check in `sendProduceRequest()` before accessing the batch:\n\n```java\nfor (ProducerBatch batch : batches) {\n    if (batch.isDone()) {\n        continue;  // Skip already completed batches\n    }\n    // ... rest of the code\n}\n```\n\nHowever, this is **not recommended** because:\n- It's a band-aid that masks the root cause (expired batches being included in the send list)\n- It's less clear that expired batches should never be sent\n- It could hide other bugs where `isDone()` is true but the batch is still sent inappropriately\n- The proposed fix is more explicit and clearer about intent\n\n### Additional Note\n\nThe comment at line 192 in `Sender.java` is relevant:\n```java\n// expireBatches is called in Sender.sendProducerData, before client.poll.\n// The !batch.isDone() invariant should always hold.\n```\n\nThis comment suggests the original intent was that expired batches would NOT be in the send list. The proposed fix restores this invariant, which is the correct approach.\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\n### The Bug in One Sentence\nA race condition in `Sender.sendProducerData()` allows deallocated buffer pools to be reused while still being referenced by batches that are sent to the network, causing message data to be corrupted with metadata from subsequent batches on different topics.\n\n### The Fix in One Sentence\nRemove expired batches from the `batches` map after deallocating their buffers, but before calling `sendProduceRequests()`, ensuring no deallocated buffers are accessed by the network layer.\n\n### Verification Steps\nTo verify this fix resolves the issue:\n\n1. Run existing test suite to ensure no regressions:\n   ```bash\n   ./gradlew clients:test --tests SenderTest\n   ./gradlew clients:test --tests RecordAccumulatorTest\n   ```\n\n3. Integration test with realistic scenario:\n   - Use a real Kafka cluster\n   - Set `linger.ms=1000` and `delivery.timeout.ms=2000`\n   - Simulate network latency/broker restart to trigger batch expiry\n   - Verify messages don't appear on unintended topics\n\n## Detailed Call Stack\n\n### Key Method Call Path for the Bug\n\n```\nSender.run() (main thread)\n  ↓\nSender.runOnce() (line ~337)\n  ↓\nSender.sendProducerData(now) (line 357-444) ← CRITICAL METHOD\n  ├─ accumulator.drain() (line 395) ← Gets batches to send\n  ├─ addToInflightBatches() (line 396) ← Adds to tracking\n  ├─ getExpiredInflightBatches() (line 406) ← Checks expiry\n  ├─ accumulator.expiredBatches() (line 407) ← Gets expired\n  │\n  ├─ for expiredBatch in expiredBatches (lines 415-423)\n  │   └─ failBatch(expiredBatch, ...) (line 418)\n  │       └─ maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch() (line 835)\n  │           └─ accumulator.deallocate(batch) (line 174)\n  │               └─ free.deallocate(buffer, capacity) (line 1032)\n  │                   ← BUFFER RETURNED TO POOL ← CRITICAL\n  │\n  └─ sendProduceRequests(batches, now) (line 442) ← BUG: Still sends expired batches\n      └─ sendProduceRequest(..., entry.getValue()) (line 858)\n          └─ for batch in batches (line 872)\n              ├─ batch.records() (line 874) ← Accesses deallocated buffer\n              └─ client.send(request) (line 914) ← Sends corrupted request\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Timeline (Normal Case - No Race Condition)\n1. User calls `producer.send(topicA, record1)`\n2. Record accumulates in RecordAccumulator\n3. `sendProducerData()` drains batches for topicA\n4. Batch is sent to network correctly\n\n### Execution Timeline (Race Condition Case)\n1. User calls `producer.send(topicA, record1)` and `producer.send(topicB, record2)`\n2. Both records accumulate\n3. `sendProducerData()` is called at `now = T0`\n4. **T0 + Δ1**: Batch for topicA is drained and added to inflight\n5. **T0 + Δ2**: Batch for topicB is drained and added to inflight\n6. **T0 + Δ3**: System clock advances (simulate delay/network lag)\n7. **T0 + Δ4**: Check for expired batches\n   - Batch for topicA has **createdMs = T0 - (linger.ms + 100ms)** (was lingering)\n   - Now **now = T0 + 500ms**, so it exceeds delivery timeout\n   - `getExpiredInflightBatches()` finds topicA batch as expired\n8. **T0 + Δ5**: `failBatch(topicA_batch)` is called\n   - `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` deallocates topicA_batch's buffer\n   - Buffer returned to pool, marked as available\n9. **T0 + Δ6**: New user call: `producer.send(topicC, record3)`\n   - RecordAccumulator allocates a new batch from the pool\n   - **Gets the same ByteBuffer** that was just deallocated from topicA_batch\n   - Writes topicC records to this buffer\n10. **T0 + Δ7**: `sendProduceRequests()` is called\n    - Includes the topicA_batch in the list (it wasn't removed from `batches` map)\n    - Tries to send topicA_batch.records()\n    - The buffer now contains topicC data and metadata\n    - **Request is serialized with topicA batch object metadata but topicC buffer content**\n    - Message intended for topicA appears on topicC\n\n### Why This Happens In Bursts\n\nThe symptom notes state: \"messages published to topic A occasionally appear on topic B instead. The corruption is rare but occurs in bursts, typically during broker restarts or network disruptions.\"\n\nThis makes sense because:\n- **Bursts during broker restarts**: When a broker restarts, in-flight batches may experience timeout conditions more frequently\n- **Bursts during network disruptions**: Batches timeout while requests are in flight, but the network layer hasn't fully transmitted them yet\n- **Rare occurrences**: The race condition requires:\n  1. A batch to expire (reach delivery timeout)\n  2. While another batch is being created and allocated from the pool\n  3. Before the expired batch's request is fully serialized to the network\n  4. This is a tight timing window, hence \"occasional\"\n\n### Buffer Lifecycle Issue\n\nThe core issue is the **buffer lifecycle mismatch**:\n- **BufferPool assumption**: Once `deallocate()` is called, the buffer is no longer in use\n- **Sender assumption**: Batches in the `batches` map are still valid after expiration check\n- **Result**: The buffer can be reused while the Sender still references it\n\n### Why CRC Passes\n\nThe Kafka protocol structure has:\n- **Per-record CRC**: Covers key, value, headers, attributes, timestamp\n- **Does NOT cover**: Topic name, partition number (in request header)\n\nSo when a message is redirected to the wrong topic:\n1. The per-record CRC still validates (it covers the message content, which is correct)\n2. But the request header (topic/partition) has been corrupted\n3. The message successfully writes to the wrong topic\n4. This is why the corruption goes undetected at the record level\n\n## Prevention and Related Code\n\nThe fix could also be implemented by:\n1. **Removing batches from inflight when expired**: Have `getExpiredInflightBatches()` also remove from the original `batches` map\n2. **Deferring sendProduceRequests**: Only include non-expired batches when calling `sendProduceRequests()`\n3. **Marking batches**: Flag batches as \"deallocated\" and skip them in `sendProduceRequests()`\n\nThe cleanest approach is **Option 1** (proposed above): Remove expired batches from the `batches` map after deallocating them but before sending, ensuring the contract is clear and failures are fail-safe.\n","numLines":333,"startLine":1,"totalLines":333}}}

Here are the key findings:\n\n### **Root Cause Identified**\n- **File**: `Sender.java` \n- **Function**: `sendProducerData(long now)` (lines 395-442)\n- **Bug Type**: Time-of-Check-Time-of-Use (TOCTOU) race condition\n\n### **The Bug Mechanism**\n\nThe bug occurs in this sequence:\n\n1. **Line 395**: Batches are drained from the accumulator\n2. **Line 396**: Batches are added to in-flight tracking\n3. **Lines 406-408**: Expired batches are identified (including in-flight batches)\n4. **Line 418**: `failBatch()` deallocates the buffer and returns it to the pool\n5. **Line 442**: `sendProduceRequests()` still tries to send the expired batches\n\nThe `batches` map is **never updated** to remove expired batches, so they're still sent to the network even though their buffers have been deallocated and returned to the pool. When a buffer is reused:\n- The batch metadata still references the original topic\n- But the buffer has been allocated to a new batch on a different topic\n- Result: Request header says \"Topic A\" but buffer contains \"Topic B\" data\n\n### **The Fix**\n\nAdd code after line 408 to remove expired batches from the `batches` map before calling `sendProduceRequests()`:\n\n```java\nif (!expiredBatches.isEmpty()) {\n    Set<ProducerBatch> expiredBatchSet = new HashSet<>(expiredBatches);\n    for (List<ProducerBatch> batchList : batches.values()) {\n        batchList.removeAll(expiredBatchSet);\n    }\n    batches.entrySet().removeIf(entry -> entry.getValue().isEmpty());\n}\n```\n\nThis ensures that no deallocated buffers are accessed by the network layer, preventing message corruption.\n\nThe complete analysis with detailed call stacks, execution timelines, and verification steps is available in `/logs/agent/solution.md`."}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":0,"cache_creation_input_tokens":5921,"cache_read_input_tokens":70025,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":5921},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"c98eb434-4b4b-4d83-b86f-2a5271c2e75b","uuid":"af6ae4a1-ea94-4f5c-8129-a17917e1800e"}
